After I have completed for you, O my sons, this book, which is the last of the science of medicine with its completion, and I have reached its end, from its expositions and its explanations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Because the operation with the hand has been destroyed in our region and in our time, completely deprived: until perhaps its science perished, and its trace was cut off: and there remained of it only small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which hands have changed: and error and hesitation happened to them, until its intentions were closed, and its force was removed: It seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this treatise in it according to the way of position, and explanation, and abbreviation: and that I should come with the forms of the instruments of the Cautery, and the other instruments of the work: when it is made from the addition of explanation, and from the haste of what is necessary.
The reason, however, why a good craftsman of it is not found with his hand in this our time, is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be exercised before that in the science of anatomy, which Galen narrated, until he knows the aids of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction, and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and muscles, and their number, and their egress, and of the pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their exit.
And because of that Hippocrates said that name with name is much, and with work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We indeed already said about that in the introduction of this book.
Because he who is not knowing what we said about anatomy, is not emptied, but already falls into error, by which men are killed: just as I saw many of those who are formed in this science, and boast of it without knowledge, and without experiment.
That is, because I saw a foolish physician incise a scrofulous abscess in the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries in the neck: wherefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to extract a stone from a man who was advanced in age, and the stone was large. Therefore he arrived at it, and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. Wherefore the man died on the third day.
And I indeed had already been called to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone, and the condition of the patient, that he would die.
And I saw another physician who received a stipend from a certain Duke of our land for medicine: and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him, a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician hastened with his ignorance, and bound the fracture over the wound with cushions and splints with a tight bandage, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he cured him according to his desires. Afterwards he dismissed him after a few days, and ordered him not to loosen the bandage: and it remained thus until his leg and his foot became suppurated, and came to destruction.
Therefore I was called to him: and I hastened to loosen the bandage: and calmness followed, and he escaped from his pains.
Nevertheless, the corruption was already established in the limb: and I could not restrain it.
Then the corruption ceased to spread in the limb, until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who perforated a cancerous abscess: and it ulcerated afterwards, until its malignancy was magnified with its master.
That is, because when a cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then it is not necessary to approach it with iron at all, unless it is in a member which can tolerate having the whole of it excised.
And therefore, O my sons, it is necessary for you to know that manual operation is divided into two divisions: namely, operation associated with safety: and operation with which there is danger in most instances.
And I have already pointed out in every place in this book where an operation occurs which involves terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to avoid it and leave it alone, so that fools may not find a way to speak and bring dishonor.
Therefore take measurements with care and caution, and treat your patients with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading by God's grace to salvation and commendable success: and leave terrible illnesses of difficult healing: and remove your minds from that which makes you fear, lest hesitation enter into your faith and your well-being.
For it is more conducive to your glory, and more sublime in this world, and finally to your rewards.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat a bad illness: lest you be called bad physicians.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise according to three Chapters.
Chapter one.
Concerning cautery with fire, and cautery with a sharp instrument, chaptered and ordered from head to foot, and the forms of instruments and tools of cautery: and everything which is necessary in the operation.
Chapter two.
Concerning incision and perforation, phlebotomy and cupping, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things to that: and the whole chaptered, ordered with the forms of instruments.
Chapter three.
Concerning restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of torsion, and similar things to that: chaptered, ordered from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
But before I recall the operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its benefits and harms: and in which complexion it should be exhibited.
Therefore I say that the discussion of the quality of the benefit of cautery, and of its harm, is a lengthy and subtle discussion, a science, and a hidden secret.
Many wise men have also spoken on it, and they have disagreed: and indeed a little from their discussions suffices me, fearing prolixity.
Therefore I say that cautery universally benefits every complexion which is with matter and without matter, except for two complexions, which are the hot complexion without matter and the dry complexion without matter.
However, in the hot and dry complexion with matter they disagreed. For some have said that cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the contrary of that, namely that cautery is not suitable in a sickness which is from heat and dryness: because the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable that a sickness from heat and dryness should be cured with heat and dryness.
And he who says the contrary said: that through cautery help is given in every hot and dry sickness which happens in the bodies of men: because when you compare the body of man and its humors to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I indeed say by his statement: because experiment has already revealed that to me several times.
Nevertheless it is not fitting that he should come to that, except he who is already proven and experienced in the chapter of cautery, by the last exercise, and has known the diversity of the complexions of men, and the disposition of sicknesses in themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and the time of them.
From the other complexions however there is no fear for you: and especially in cold and moist sicknesses. For already all physicians have agreed upon them: and they have not disagreed in helping with cautery in them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine is: because fire is simple, whose action does not arrive except to the member which is cauterized: and it does not harm another member joined with it, except with small harm.
The action of burning medicines however arrives at that which is distant from the members: and perhaps it causes sickness in a member difficult of healing, and perhaps it kills.
Fire however, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now indeed that has become known to us through experiment, because of the length of service and study with the art, and standing upon the truth of things: and because of that I excuse myself from length of speech.
And if it were not that it is not permitted to this my book, I would bring to you a hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels sicknesses with a philosophical demonstrative speech, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree in the time in which it is fitting to perform cautery, and they place the better time in spring.
And I say that cautery is fitting in every time: therefore, because harm happening because of time is submerged in the help which is drawn with cautery. And especially if cautery is because of pains from necessary, strong, urgent pains, which do not tolerate slowness: because it is feared from them that there may happen a greater harm than the small harm entering because of time.
And let not that fall into your minds, O sons, which only the common people and foolish physicians do not fear, namely that to that sickness which is healed by cautery, there is not always a return: and they place that as a consequence, and the matter is not as they think: because cautery is nothing but in place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and dries the humors which are the causes why pains happen.
Nevertheless cautery surpasses medicine by the speed of its health, and the power of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that the sickness may return at some time according to the complexion of the infirm, and the location of his sickness, and its power: and that which is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in it: and that which arrives at it in its acquisition from foods, and similar things from causes, unless the sickness is made in which cautery is administered.
A subtle sickness in a member of few superfluities and humors, such as cautery of a tooth because of pain, and similar things to it, for it is possible that that pain may not return in it. But that happens in few.
But truly the talk of the common people again, that cautery is the last of medicine, is right talk: not to that which they intend in it: because they believe that there is no cure which confers with medicine, nor with anything else after the setting of cautery.
But the matter is contrary to that, and the intention that cautery is the last of medicine is not, except that when we administer modes of cure in some sicknesses, and those medicines do not confer: then we administer cautery at the end of the matter, and it confers: then from this it falls that cautery is the last of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients however said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron: and they did not say that except because of the equality of gold, and the excellence of its substance: and they said that the place of cautery does not make pus. That is not true absolutely: because I have now proved it, and found that it does not do that in some bodies without others.
And cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you heat a cautery in fire made of gold, it is not clear to you when it is heated according to the quantity you wish, because of the redness of gold: and when it tends towards cold, and if you add to it heating, it melts in the fire, and turns into plates.
Therefore the craftsman falls from that into difficulty: and on account of that, cautery with iron is quicker and more convenient for us, because of its suitability for the operation.
And I indeed have now ordered this Chapter on Cautery, according to chapters: and I have ordered them from head to foot: so that they may relieve him who seeks what he wants from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization contributes to the control of moisture and coldness on the brain: which two are causes of headache, and of the abundance of the flow of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and of much sleep, and of toothache, and of sore throat: and universally of every illness which happens from coldness, such as paralysis, and headache, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should instruct the patient: that he be evacuated first with a cleansing purgative medicine for the head for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the patient, and his age, and his habit require.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then have him sit between your hands squarely, so that he has placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger reaches, mark that place with ink.
Then heat the olive cautery; its form is this.
Then place it upon the place marked with ink, descending, so that your hand is gradually tightened, and you will roll it. Then quickly lift your hand and look at the place.
If you see now revealed from the bone the quantity of the head of alkiel, or the quantity of zeuherbi, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat with your hand the iron itself, or with another if it cools, until you see the bones which I told you about.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water, and soak the cautery in it, and place it on the place; and leave it for three days.
Then place on it the cautery soaked in butter, and leave it on the place until the burn is destroyed. Then treat it with tetrapharmacon ointment until it is healed.
Now they have said that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it emits; wherefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized to the bone, and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of the bone is burned.
Then scrape away what has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to reach the bone with the cautery until it makes a strong impression on the bone, so that the bone falls away, which is made like the form of a kirate: or an instrument which women place in a small alphabet infusion: and they think that vapours from the head are exhaled from this place, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then treat it until it heals.
But to me these two types of cautery do not seem at all suitable except in certain men, according to the way of fear.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better for his health.
For the head is weakened by the disruption of its natural continuity: as we have testified in other members: and especially when the head of the sick person is naturally weak: and indeed the first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it: therefore operate with it safely.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs in the whole head: and it is prolonged in the sick person, and he uses bloodlettings, and cuppings, and purgatives for the head, and oils, and poultices. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we have described, and none of those things benefit him: then consider. For if the patient's head is of strong natural constitution, and is not weak, and finds intense cold: then cauterize with another cautery a little below that one. Then cauterize it above every horn of his head with a cautery, until the skin is not pierced, and a quantity of bone, as we have described, is uncovered. And cauterize it with one cautery in the occiput of his head, in the place which is called the vessel: and it is the place where a cupping glass is placed: and raise your cautery in this, and do not uncover the bone. For the patient finds a very intense pain because of that, and different from the pain of all the other cauterizations of the head.
And I will say this: the cautery in its place; and it is necessary that the cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and its occiput, be finer than the cautery with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and throbbing occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is evacuated with cleansing medicines, and the remaining treatment which I described in the divisions of illnesses is administered, and all this does not help: then cauterization is indicated in two ways: either cauterization with a sharp burning medicine or with iron.
Cauterization with a sharp burning medicine is done as follows: take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut off its ends on both sides. Then incise the painful area at the time with a wide phlebotomy knife until a space is made under the skin, into which the clove is inserted.
Then insert it under the skin until it is hidden; then bind it with a suitable compress and leave it for fifteen hours; then unbind it and remove the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days; afterwards apply a poultice steeped in butter until the place produces pus; then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, do it with some burning medicines, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, On Burning Medicines.
Cauterization with an iron, however, is done in this way. A fire cautery, whose form is this.
And it is called a nail because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it there is a small prominence.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand; and you slowly revolve the iron with speed; and let the amount which is burned be of the thickness of the skin, about half of it. And raise your hand, so that the artery which is below is not burned, and a flow of blood does not occur.
Then soak a pledget in salt water, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; then apply a pledget with butter; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second knife-like extremity of the cautery. And beware of cutting the artery in this hemicrania, not properly the old one.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in an old hemicrania.
When you treat a hemicrania, with what we have said from the preceding treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and the treatment does not help: and you see from the illness that what we have said is not sufficient, neither the first cautery with medicine, nor cautery with fire, then it is necessary that you heat the knife-like cautery until it turns white after you mark on the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or thereabouts: and put down your hand at once, and press it until you cut the artery, and reach to the bone.
Nevertheless it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jaw, which moves in mastication, lest the side be burned, or the nerve which moves it, whence a spasm may result.
And be watchful and cautious about the flow of blood from the artery which has been cut. For in its incision there is danger, and especially to him who is ignorant of what he does, and is neither studious nor experienced: and he leaves the operation with it in the first instance.
And I shall come with a recollection of the regime of the flow of blood happening from an artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
But if you see from the sickness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery which we described in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with a cautery having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in earache.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold, and it is treated with resolvents and the other treatment which we described in the division, and the pain is not removed, then cauterize with fire; and it is that which is called a point, whose form is this.
Then make points with it after its ignition around the whole ear, as it is rolled around; or around both, if the pain is in both at the same time. And move the cautery away from the root of the ear a little, after you have marked the places with the cautery; and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points in each ear, and about that.
Then treat the places until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in torticollis.
Chapter VII.
Torticollis which is cured with cauterization is only from the species which happen from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterization of the species which happens from desiccation and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this species of torticollis with bleedings, and purgatives, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little lower than its temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the affected part. Because softening does not happen except in the part which appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with a cautery directly at the end of the upper ear under the horn of the head a little: and another in the temple: whose length is according to the length of a thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a kind of knife, whose form has been described; however, it is not a little thinner than that, as you see: and it is necessary that there be a little excess thickness in the knife.
Then take care of the place, with what preceded, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes chronic, and you treat it with what we have said, and your treatment does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on each horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we have said, and with a cautery in the occiput of the head, according to what preceded: and the method of cauterization should be according to what preceded.
Also, cauterize with a cautery above the stomach; and this is more of a last resort.
Then let him be treated with what preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the beginning large amounts of hyera be given to the sick person in a drink, and pills that cleanse the brain.
Then shave the whole head of the sick person, and place on the back of his head a plaster of mustard described in the treatise on plasters; and apply it several times.
For this is the method of cauterization: and do it according to the same order which I described there.
If therefore he is healed by it, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauterizations in the posterior part of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cauterization the breadth of a finger.
Then treat the cauterization, with that which preceded.
But if you wish an addition, and the patient is able to tolerate it: then make for him a cauterization in the middle. But if you wish an addition: then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then treat it until it is healed: and let the cauterization be oiled according to the form which was previously described.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed in the cleansing of the head with sponges, and with that which we have said.
Then shave the head of the sick person; afterward cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery upon each horn of the head, and with a cautery upon the posterior part of it, and with three upon the vertebrae of the neck.
But if you need in the sickness a softening of the body with more of those things, and the infirm person is tolerant, and the sickness is strong: then cauterize him with four cauteries upon the vertebrae of the back, and finally with a cautery, until a great deal of his skin is burned, and raise your hand. Then take care of him until he is healed: and thus cauterize Oliuare.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you first cleanse his brain with bleedings and with the other treatment which we have described in the division: when the patient is strong, or is tolerant in receiving medicines.
But if he is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and mouthwashes cleansing the brain are administered beforehand for many days, with improvement of diet.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the manner: and with another cautery in his occiput, and over every horn of his head with a cautery. But if the patient is strong and is tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I mentioned in the case of one having paralysis and softening of the body, over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back: and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner which preceded.
But if the patient is a child, then apply a small cautery, according to this manner.
Concerning the method of cauterization in melancholia.
When the cause of melancholia is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we mentioned in the case of one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholia is a superfluity inclined towards melancholia, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink which will cleanse his brain, according to what preceded in the division: then shave the head of the patient, and afterwards make a properly made compress of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the patient sitting squarely should be held on all sides.
Then present the liniment. And it is more worthy from old sheep butter. And heat it over a fire with a moderate measured heat, which the finger can tolerate when put into it. Then empty it in the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do this for the patient once every week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it making very many small points of it, except that you hold your hand with the cautery: indeed it is by smelling.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with a quality.
Then place on it a piece of cloth soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a descending flow of water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs which I mentioned in the division, then begin and purge the patient with that which cleanses his head.
And keep him from all dampness, and make him sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then order him to shave his head, and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him above the two temples with two cauteries, if the beginning of the descent of water is in both eyes simultaneously: or from one side, if the beginning of water is in one eye: and cut off with the cautery all the veins and arteries which are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in the width of the temples: and beware of a flow of blood.
But if you see something of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and the cutting off of them, and caution from a flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries ultimately produced.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old, constant: and are upon the veins and arteries which are in the exterior of the head manifest, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities: then cauterize with the same cautery which I narrated in the beginning of the descending water, with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries upon the two temples, and with two cauteries in the neck under the two bones. And if you need addition, then cauterize it on every side cautiously of the eye, above the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in nasal stench.
When you treat it with what we said in the division, and the medication does not help: then hasten, and give the patient theriac in drink for three nights; then shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle with an olive-shaped cautery. Then cauterize it with a nail-shaped cautery, with two cauteries, above the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And beware of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the shape of the nail-shaped cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterization in softening the eyelid.
When the eyelid is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries in each part; and let them be distant from the two temples; and let the length of each cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not move your hand with the cautery too much, but according to the amount that burns a third of the eyelid.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs turn inwards, pricking the eye.
Cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with fire, or cauterization with a burning medicine.
In cauterization with fire, however, instruct the patient beforehand to remove his hairs, if he is one of those who remove them, until they are lengthened and made even. But if they prick him at their root, then bind his eyes with a fillet, so that they do not move, until they grow.
When therefore they grow and are even, then place the patient's head in your bosom; then mark upon the eyelid of his eyes with a hot iron, a mark which is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a pledget soaked in egg white or in flaxseed mucilage upon the eye.
Then fire the cautery, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the mark which you made, little by little in many times, until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burnt, properly appearing.
And the sign of the health of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye now contract, and the hairs rise up near the puncture of the eye.
Raise your hand then and leave it for three days.
Then place on it lint with butter, until the eschar is eradicated. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
But if some of the hairs return after a time, and the eyelid softens, then repeat the cautery on that place, as you did at first.
But if the hairs are below, then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place and is even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is so that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even. Make from paper or cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take of known soap and of unslaked lime, one ounce of each or thereabouts; then grind them together well and do this quickly so that it does not become cold. Then spread some of it on the paper which you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a piece of cotton soaked in egg white; and let the patient's head be in your bosom.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it gently. And you should move it whenever the patient feels the medicine biting; for its bite is found to be like fire.
While therefore the biting which he feels persists, then remove the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid raised, as it is raised by burning with fire, or with incision, it is well: and if not, then apply more of the medicine to the place where the medicine does not bite and blacken, until your operation is even, and the eye is contracted.
Then place a compress with butter on it, until the burnt skin is eradicated. Then treat it with diaphnincon ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to observe the utmost care, lest anything of the medicine fall into the eye.
But if the eyelid softens afterwards, and something fights from the hairs in the eye, then repeat the medicine on that place which softens from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be: and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who studies this art.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a lachrymal fistula.
When you treat a fistula, with what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment does not help: then, it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your bosom, and let a servant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it is not moved or shaken.
Then place a cotton pledget soaked in egg white or in flaxseed mucilage over his eye; then heat the cautery, whose shape is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's quill from one end, with which the cautery is made: and if you wish it to be penetrating to the other end, and if you wish it to be upward, try it thus.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then press the fistula, if it is open, and draw out the pus from it, and dry it: and if it is not open, then open it, and draw out its pus.
Then place the cautery, made very hot, upon it.
And hold your hand with it a little near the cautery from the eye, towards the side of the nose, so that your hand does not err, or the patient be disturbed: and place the cautery on the fat of the eye, and destroy it.
If therefore you reach with the beginning of your cautery to the bone, it will be well. And if not, then repeat the cautery once, or twice, if you need it: and leave it for three days.
Then apply a pledget with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment, until it is healed.
But if forty days have passed, and it is not healed: then put on it a sharp corrosive medicine, until the bone is exposed: and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which certain earlier ones mentioned. Apply to the place of the fistula, and incise it: then place in the incision a fine tube, that is, a fine cannula, of which this is the shape. And pour into it the quantity of a drachm of melted lead, and hold your hand with good retention of the cannula, and let the patient not move at all, lest the melted lead run, or reach his eye.
And it is necessary that you place over the patient's eye a compress soaked in egg white, or in water.
For the lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we have said, by cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer to the opening of the nose, and to reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come in its own proper place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing fissures of the lips.
Fissures, which are called chaps, often occur on the lip, and especially on the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures with what we have said in the division of illnesses, and the treatment does not help, then cauterize with a small, knife-like cautery, according to this form.
And let its concavity be according to the thinness of a knife.
Then quickly apply the heated instrument to the fissures themselves until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with cerate until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus, and breaks; afterwards it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and a fistula forms; then you treat it, and the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that you apply a cautery according to the size it occupies in the fistula. Then insert the heated cautery into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and its end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said concerning treatment until it is cured.
If therefore the pus is excised, and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place, and to remove the corrupt bone according to what comes into its head.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the gums and softened teeth.
When the gum is softened because of humors, and the teeth are loosened, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not help: then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then a cautery of fire, whose form will come after this, so that you place a cannula upon the tooth: and quickly insert the ignited cautery into it: and hold your hand a little while, until the sick person feels the heat of the fire already having reached the root of the tooth.
And lift your hand; then repeat the cautery several times, as you wish.
Then let the sick person fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For the loosened tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupt humor is dried.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for toothache.
When toothache is due to coldness, or there is cold or a worm in the tooth, and treatment with medicines is not helpful: then cauterization is appropriate in two ways: either cauterization with butter, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with butter is done as follows: take cow's butter, and boil it in an iron spoon or in a pan. Then take a tent, and wrap it around the end of a probe. Then dip it in the boiling butter: and quickly apply it to the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools; then repeat this several times, until the effect of the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool or a tent in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth; and place a red-hot iron on top of it, until the fire penetrates to the depth of the tooth's cavity.
Cauterization with fire is done by aiming at a bronze or iron tube. And let there be something of thickness in its body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then heat the cautery, whichever form it may be: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or on another.
And it is necessary in the impression of that cautery, that the patient fill his mouth with good butter, and hold it for one hour: then spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish, according to what is possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in strumae.
When strumae are from phlegm and from cold humors, and are not obedient to digestion through medicines, and you wish their digestion quickly: then a concave cautery of fire, whose form is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may exit from the cautery from the other end: and place it ignited upon the abscess once, and a second time if you need it, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
But if the abscess is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it lint infused in butter, until what the fire burned is removed.
Then treat it with tooth unguent, until the form of a tube is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in hoarseness of voice, and constriction of breath.
When humors overcome the lung canal, and especially when it is with coldness of complexion, then it is necessary that the sick person be evacuated first with solutive medicines.
Then cauterize it in the throat at the root of the throat in a depressed place: and beware, lest you arrive with the cautery at the throat, nor in the skin, except a little of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the joint of the neck in the last vertebra of it, making an end: and let the cautery be nail-shaped according to the manner which preceded.
Then treat it with that which preceded, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in diseases of the lung, and cough.
When cough and lung disease are from cold humors, and the infirm person does not have a fever, nor consumption, and the disease is of long standing: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the clavicle in places depressed, soft, and empty. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be a cannula according to the form which preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by puncturing with a cautery, which is called Punctum, whose form preceded in the puncturing of earache: and let the points be from thirty points up to about others.
Then treat him with what preceded, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore the cauterization is alleviated with it, when you do with it at once three cauterizations.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated by reason of humors, and is not fixed in the hour of its return from its dislocation, until it is accustomed to return, then it is dislocated by a small movement, which happens as we have already testified, then it is necessary that you reduce the dislocation in the first place. Then the patient is laid on his back, or on his healthy side. Then raise the skin which is in the inner armpit upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then have a cautery with two points. Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates it to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three points, wherefore the figure of the cauterization then becomes six cauteries: and the points are according to the thinness of a probe.
And this is the form of a cautery having three points.
And sometimes one is added in this manner, wherefore there are eight cauteries.
Then put crushed leeks with salt on the cautery. Then cause the patient to adhere to stillness, so that the limb is not moved for some time, until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is towards the upper parts, and rarely does that happen, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a nail-shaped cautery, or with many cauteries by puncturing.
For the joint is strengthened, and the moisture is removed: and the patient is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When coldness and much moisture occur in the stomach, until they draw it away from its complexion, and catarrhs are multiplied to it, and frequent methods of treatment do not help: then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back, and extend his legs and his hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the breastbone the size of one finger with a nail-shaped cautery, and two cauteries below on the two sides of one cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And separate them from each other so that they do not join, when they produce pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery by which this cautery is made be one according to the figure of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by puncturing it for him who is frightened by this cautery: and it is so that you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity which you wish with a hot iron: then cauterize it with a pointed cautery: then cure it with the cure which preceded until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When pain occurs in the liver from coldness and dampness, or from gross flatulence, until it departs from its natural complexion by superfluous departure, and the sick person is cured with what we have said, and it does not benefit him: then it is necessary that the sick person be laid supine upon his neck, and you mark with a hot iron three cauteries according to this figure, and this same quantity upon the lower liver from the hypochondria, where the elbow of a man reaches: and let the space which is between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be according to the length of a straight body: and do not press your hand with the cautery very much.
And let the quantity of what is burned be of the thickness of the skin, the quantity of half of it not added: and let the sick person be standing on his feet.
But if he is not standing, then let him be lying, who now extends his legs and raises his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is indeed possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a knife-cautery, when you have skill and prudence in the art.
And beware that you do not proceed excessively in cauterization, and the thickness of the whole skin is burned, wherefore the whole body is burned, and it reaches the intestines: because the skin there is thin, therefore know that.
Concerning the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When an exit occurs, and you wish to know if that abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the sick person experiences pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is intense sharpness with the pain: and you see now that its treatment has wearied the physicians.
Therefore, it is necessary that the sick person lie on his back. Then mark the location of the abscess with a cautery; then heat a cautery that resembles a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery until the whole skin is burned and it reaches the siphac, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment of exits, until it is healed.
And it is not necessary to use this type of cautery except by one whose study in the art of medicine is prolonged, and through whose hands these illnesses occur with experiment many times: then indeed let him dare this operation.
But truly, to leave it, is better with me.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in pleurisy.
The ancients said, cautery with the roots of aristolochia for cold pleurisy in this manner. And it is, that you receive of the long dried roots of aristolochia, one longer root, which is found in it, and let it be like the thickness of a finger. Then submerge it in oil: and ignite it in the fire. Then cauterize with one cautery in that which is between the continuation of the clavicle with the neck, and with two small cauteries somewhat sloping below the chin toward the part which is under the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth rib somewhat sloping towards the back: and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one in that which is between the two shoulder blades: and with two cauteries on the two sides of the chest, lower than the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary that you press your hand with the cautery, rather let it be evident on the skin by smelling.
And now some ancients have said that there are some men who use a cautery of iron similar to a ray: and they ignite it, and internally they put it into that which is between the ribs, until it arrives with it at the abscess, and pus comes out: just as we said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with a cautery there is fear that either the patient dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no healing.
Chapter XXXII. On the method of cauterizing the spleen.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, with what we have said of treatment in the division of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then cauterization in it is according to three methods, which are all correct.
One of which is, that you make three cauteries, or four, lining up according to the length of the spleen according to the figure of the liver cauteries, the figure of which preceded.
And let there be between each cautery the quantity of the thickness of a finger, or a little more or less.
And let the method of cautery be, as we said in the cautery of the liver, equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the patient be lying on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: that you heat a cautery having two prongs, which we mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of the humerus: and lift the skin, which is in the direction of the spleen, where the patient's left elbow reaches: and let your elevation by which you lift the skin be according to the breadth of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert two very hot prongs until you penetrate the skin on the other side with them: then withdraw the cautery: therefore four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then take care of the cautery after you dismiss it, that it discharges pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than the rest which preceded from the treatment.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in dropsy.
Cauterization does not fall in dropsy, except for ascites specifically.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment which we described in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery above the stomach, and another cautery above the liver, and a cautery above the spleen, and two cauteries on the back between the vertebrae, and one in the region of the chest, and another in the region of the stomach: and let the depth of the cautery be approximately the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, so that it may discharge pus for a long time.
And do not remove the patient from treatment after cauterization with it: for it is necessary that two intentions be combined for him; and healing will hasten to him with Gods help.
However, the shape of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized, should be nail-shaped: according to what preceded as to its form; and that with which the back is cauterized, should be olive-shaped according to what preceded as to its form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When abscesses occur in a dropsical patient, and are filled with yellowish water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the hollow which is between the little finger and the ring finger; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then raise your hand; and do not repeat it at all.
For the yellowish water will sweat out, and let the cautery be according to this form.
Then make on the two legs two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the knife-like end of the cautery; and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and another lower than that, about the middle of the leg; and on each hip two cauteries; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water may sweat out from it; then treat it with the other things which we have mentioned.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in looseness of the bowels.
Chapter 35.
When there is looseness of the bowels from cold and humors, until it weakens the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with methods of treatment, and is not healed; and you see the patient tolerating cauterization of exuberant virtue, then cauterize him with a large cautery over his stomach, as preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four small cauteries around the navel, with a small nail-like cautery; and a cautery over the alcatin above the alhosos, a large one, or two cauteries.
And if you see exuberant humors, and the patient tolerating it, then cauterize him with a cautery over the pubis, and a cautery over each ilium; and perhaps you will add two small cauteries over the stomach near the large one.
For it is a beneficial treatment, whose help does not err.
Concerning the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupt humors, and they are treated with that which we said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries over the lower vertebra of the back below the almond somewhat triangularly, and with a cautery below the navel as if with two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face breaking out, then cauterize him over the stomach with a large cautery, according to what preceded: and cauterize over his liver, and another over his spleen, with a nail-shaped cautery: and leave the cautery open for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut away althelul, then you heat a cautery that resembles a ray. Then insert it, burning, into the excised althelul: and move your hand until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows: do this once or twice.
If therefore the althelul are many, then cauterize each one with a cautery according to what we have narrated. Then treat them with that which helps them of ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over the alcatin, it is more ultimate in aid.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the patient does not obey the incision and the operation which we have described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he is healed with a cautery.
Therefore, when a fistula occurs in someone, and it becomes old, pus and corrupt humors run from it. It is therefore more fitting that you should probe it with a slender probe. Then ascertain the amount of its depth with a probe.
Then heat a cautery which is similar to a ray. Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula and to the extent that the nail entered.
And repeat the cautery over it until all those corrupt bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the amount of your need.
And guard yourself from burning a nerve, if it is there, or a large vein: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then guard yourself from all these places.
And do not do this except when the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it is healed.
But if the place is sealed, and the materials are cut away from it, and it remains so for a long time: then know that it is now completely healed.
And if materials are not cut away from it, then know that it is penetrating, or in its depth there is a corrupt bone, or something like that from those: the remembrance of which will come in its place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold or from thick wind, and the patient's strength is diminished because of it, then it is necessary to cauterize it above the almethen above the kidneys, cauterizing over each kidney with a nail-shaped cautery, the remembrance of which has preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time in the almeidatu itself. Therefore, three lines will result. Therefore, the last will be more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening occur in the bladder from cold and moisture, until the sick person does not retain urine, then cauterize it in the lower part of the pubis above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubis begin, and with a cautery from the right of the pubis, and another from the left of it: and let the length of that lateral cauterization be according to the size of the thumb's joint: and cauterize it with a lower dorsal cautery, or with two cauteries, if you need it: and let the cautery be according to what preceded, namely a nail-shaped cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the womb, and it is prevented by that from impregnation, and her menses are corrupted, and their provocation is delayed, and pain occurs to her at their arrival, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery above the pubis lower on the back, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be nail-shaped.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous humors are poured out to the socket of the hip, and they become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of that is, that the leg is lengthened over the other, when they are compared to each other: and the place of the dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the patient over the socket of his hip with a cautery similar to a circle: after you mark with a hot iron around the socket, as it is rolled: and that the socket itself fall in the middle of the circle.
But if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive-shaped cautery: and let the depth of the cautery be according to the quantity of the thickness of all the skin.
Then take care of it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and humors, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it becomes chronic, then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or with artificial pills, and the like. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with burning medicines, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is, that you cauterize above the hip joint itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make them a good, or bad, depth. And let the space which is between each cautery be the size of the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes, however, a cautery is made in the middle above the head of the hip joint itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, with one: so that it is a circle containing the whole hip.
And burn the thickness of the whole skin.
This is the method of cauterization in sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
But if it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries above the thigh, above the place to which the sick person points there, in which there is pain, and with your cautery above the ankle four fingers towards the outside slightly: and let the cautery be knife-shaped.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
But if the sick person indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a pointed cautery, three, or four, or more, if it needs that.
And if he indicates the pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with one knife-shaped cautery.
And beware in all your cauterization, that you do not go so far with the cautery as to burn a nerve, or a large artery, and draw upon the sick person through that a bad harm, or contraction.
And I indeed have already seen one and another, of those who cauterized above the ankle, and went too far in cauterization, and the leg swelled, until the swelling reached the foot, and it was completely perforated, and the whole foot was corrupted: then there occurred a looseness of the bowels, and death after that.
But if the pain is in two parts at the same time, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men have said concerning the cauterization of the hip, of which cautery this is the method. Make a similar iron cautery, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date-stone, or somewhat less: and within that cautery let there be a third cautery.
And let the space which is between each cautery be the quantity of a thumb-joint: and let the cauteries be open on two sides: and let their height be like a joint, or two joints: and make for them a handle of iron decently fitted to the cauteries.
Then let it be heated in the fire until it glows red and throws off sparks; then let it be placed upon the hip-joint, the patient lying on his sound side. Therefore cauterize him with three round cauteries at once.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply plasters with butter, and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, "My son, we have used this type of cautery little, because of the terror of its appearance, and because we have found few who would endure it.
However, it is one of the good cauteries for him who endures it, and finds with it its place.
The cautery with burning medicines is made as follows: you make two plates having a perforated ring into which descends a hinge of its door made of bronze or iron, the length of the wall; at the height of which are two knots or similar things.
And let the space which is between both be the amount of the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above; and let that which contains itself together be according to this form.
Then place it over the hip joint, the patient lying on the healthy side. And press your hand very much upon the hip joint. Then pour between the two circles warm water which has been heated a little with fire, and hold it for the amount of an hour; and let the patient tolerate its biting and burning, for he will find the biting like fire, until the biting ceases.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and wipe the warm water from the whole hip with fresh water; then leave it for three days.
And put butter on it until the blackness of the burn is removed; and leave it for several days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the final help.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
But if the pain extends to the hip or leg, make him sit in that which contains water, according to what you did to the hip equally.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, one part of each; grind both, and put them in a new pot, the bottom part of which is perforated with one small hole, according to the size that the ray may enter it; and place under the bottom of the pot another glass pot; and pour over the alkali and lime some fresh water, so that it submerges both by a finger's breadth; after which you compress them with your hand with good pressure; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends to the bottom of the glass pot.
Then collect all that water, and pour it over more lime; and filter it until it is renewed.
For then it will be of very strong sharpness, which is used in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of other members. Because it produces the operation of fire itself.
And among medicines are those with which ankles are cauterized, also like testicle, and cashew apple honey, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed.
And Galen indeed, in narrating, recounted the cure of a certain man from antiquity, by which he was cured of pain in the hip and sciatic vein; and he magnified it to be very great. And he said that he did not need another cure, and that he was healed in one time, until he recounted that he perhaps entered a bath carried, and came out of it already healed.
And it is so that it is taken from fresh setaragi; and if fresh is not found, let dry, recent, be taken; and let it be ground much with some fat, and let it be placed upon the hip, where there is pain, or leg, or in the thigh; and let it be bound, and let it be left for the amount of three hours, or for the amount that the infirm person feels a lessening of burning. Then introduce him into the bath.
Therefore, when his body becomes dewy, introduce him to the seat. For the pain recedes, and it is healed.
And know that it is not fitting that anyone use a cautery with these medicines except after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides also said that goat dung, when the sciatic vein is cauterized with it, benefits it: and the cautery is made in this way. Let wool be taken, and let it be soaked in old oil, and let it be placed upon the deep place which is between the thumb of the foot and the ankle bone, and is nearer to the ankle bone.
Then take dry goat dung, and burn it in the fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then put it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat it. Therefore do not cease doing this, until feeling comes to the middle as far as the ankle, and the pain rests.
And this method of cauterization is called the Vaccine cautery.
Concerning the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from a fall, or from a blow, or from superfluous evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and moist matter; and cauterization indeed does not fall, except in this single species, which occurs from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuation of the patient with foul-smelling pills and the like, so that three lines are made on the back where the pain is, according to the width of the almond itself, after you mark with encaustic in each line five cauteries, or more according to the amount that comes from the patient's tolerance by virtue of him: and let cauterization be done with a pointed cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize with three cauteries, or four, with a nail-shaped cautery in the middle, according to this form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in incipient gibbosity.
This illness often happens to small infants.
And a sign of its beginning in children is that a constriction occurs in breathing upon elevation and movement; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and its knots that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see it and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular in this form.
And let the cautery take in all parts of the vertebra equally; and if you wish to cauterize around the vertebra with a pointed cautery, make two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware lest you apply the cautery to a hump which is caused by a spasm of the nerve.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in gout and the pains of the joints.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humors which are poured out into any limbs of the body, then when pains happen in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call this properly gout.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of cure, and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is so that one cauterizes him after evacuation around the joint of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to puncture on the surface of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. But if the pains ascend to the knees, or the other joints, and this happens many times, then cauterize it above each knee with three cauteries, or four on every side, with this same Clavus cautery.
If moreover more are necessary with this cautery, then cauterize it. And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and the back: then administer what we said of the cautery in its chapter.
But if the pains are in the hands only, then puncture around the wrists, as two lines are revolved.
But if pain remains in the fingers, then puncture them, above every knot a puncture, and above the ridge of the hand.
But if the pains ascend after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every part.
And do not remove the patient from a good regimen, from the reception of medicines. For if a good regimen is made, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with God's help with this cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groins, and the intestine or scrotum descends to the testicle, and it is beginning nearby: then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to omit eating on his day. And that he use lenitives, so that stool descends from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and instruct him to hold his breath, until the scrotum or intestine emerges or appears.
Then return it with your fingers, and mark with a cautery under the rupture above the pubic bone, with a mark whose end is similar to half a circle towards the upper parts of the body.
Then heat the cautery, whose form is this, until it becomes white, and throws off sparks. Then return the intestine or scrotum to its concavity. Then let the assistant place his hand on the place, so that the intestine does not come out: and you will have opened between the legs of the patient, and placed a cushion under him, and another assistant over his legs, and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery over that mark, your hand with the cautery standing straight. And hold it until you reach the bone with it; or repeat with it another time, if you did not reach the bone with it in the first attempt.
And carefully observe the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and this brings about death or great harm to the patient.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your operation is not effective.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be thin, according to their size.
Then treat with other ointments until it is healed.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you give him nourishment for the length of time of his treatment, which softens his bowels: so that the intestine does not come out during straining and evacuation.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then apply a properly made bandage, and let him keep it on for another forty days.
And let him be lessened from labor, and from fullness of food and drink, and from loud voices.
For when he uses this regime, thus he is healed with a complete healing.
And I will describe the treatment of ruptures with incision in its chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen, and are beginning, and you wish that they not increase, then cauterize his rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burned be then as a third of it. Then treat him with what we have said: and it will not increase.
And now some earlier ones have said: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with a branding iron, and a line is placed which is across the upper side of the rupture, and another line to the lower. And place your hand in the middle with a nail-shaped cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterization in pains due to a fall or blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in some member from a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help it, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of every member be according to its size, and its suitability, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twisting, and the pain from it.
If therefore it heals from the first cauterization, it is well. If not, then repeat the cauterization on it.
Because it is customary for these pains to move from one member to that which is near it. Therefore it is necessary that you pursue them with cautery, until the sick person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
Lepers, however, are sometimes helped by cautery with the greatest benefit. And especially the type of leprosy which arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore when you wish to cauterize it, consider.
If therefore the leprosy is incipient, and you have treated it with what we have said in the division, and it does not subside nor remain static: and you fear for the patient, that corruption will seize upon his whole constitution: then cauterize him upon the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the noted head, and a second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two upon the two temples, and one behind upon the nape of the neck.
And lastly, apply your hand with the cautery lightly, until it imprints a small mark on the skin, and the outer layers are separated from it: so that the exhalation of thick vapours from it is relieved, and cauterize also with the cautery upon the spleen itself, as has preceded.
But if the leprosy is already spread over the patient, and is manifestly apparent: then it is necessary that you cauterize with those cauteries which we have mentioned on the head, and with a cautery upon the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries upon the two cheekbones, and with two cauteries upon the vertebrae of the neck, and six upon the vertebrae of the back, and one large one upon the haunch near the coccyx and one above it, in the almeidati: and two upon the hips: namely upon each hip one, and two upon the knees: one upon each knee, and two upon the shoulders, and two upon the elbows, and two upon the soft parts of his chest: and cauterize him upon every joint, of the joints of his fingers and toes: and cauterize upon every heel of his feet, and the wrists of his hands.
And beware of the nerves which are upon the back of the heel, lest you burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery upon the pubic bone, and another upon the stomach, and another upon the liver.
And know that the more you add cautery, the more help there is, and the more beneficial it is.
And know that the patient does not find pain in cauterization, as healthy people find it: because his body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of size and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to what preceded in the kinds of instruments.
Then treat the cautery with the flour of an herb with honey, and the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in numbness.
When a limb is numb, and is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize that numb limb with cauteries, according to what the size or smallness of the limb deserves.
And let your cautery penetrate a little into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes cauterization is done for a certain numbness which happens in the hand and foot, in the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves which move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
Truly, let no one presume upon this except he who is wise in the anatomy of the limbs, and the exit of the nerves moving the body.
Chapter 51.
When Albaras becomes chronic and nothing from the arts of medicine benefits it, then cauterize over it with a deep cautery slightly, according to the amount of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed.
Then treat it with the flour of the herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and pigeon's blood, and swallow's blood: of each let there be one part; let all these be mixed, and spread upon a cloth, and applied to the place, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Cancer.
When cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it is rolled up.
The wise, however, have said that it should be cauterized with a hot cautery in the middle.
But it does not seem so to me, because I fear that it will ulcerate; and I have already seen that many times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we have said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Adubelati.
When someone has an adubelati, and it is delayed in maturation, either because of the superfluity causing it, or because of the age of the patient, when he is decrepit and has little blood, or because of time, and one wishes to hasten the maturation of the adubelati, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, puncturing. Then leave it. For it itself will hasten with maturation.
But if you wish its perforation with a cautery, then a fire cautery, of which this is the form.
And place it in the middle of the adubelati, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from that which follows the infirmity, so that the flow of pus may be relieved.
Then care for it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a corroding ulcer.
Chapter 54.
A corroding ulcer is nothing but a corruption in a limb which moves, and corrodes it: just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore if you see a corroding ulcer in a place which can tolerate cauterization with fire, then cauterize it with fire, many small and large nails, according to what is suitable for the place in which the corroding ulcer is.
Then cauterize it on every side until you eradicate the whole corruption, and nothing at all of it remains.
Then leave it for three days, and apply to the cauterized places ground sulfur with oil, until all the eschars and all the corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments which generate flesh.
Therefore if you see that after three days flesh grows in a healthy way, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then repeat the cautery on that which remains of the corrupted places.
And a corrosive is sometimes treated with a sharp medicine. For it itself arises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of quicker help: and I indeed have already spoken of its cauterization with a sharp medicine in the division: therefore accept it there when you need it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Clavi and Warts.
Chapter 55.
Often this illness happens in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, hardened thing which harms the foot.
And indeed cautery in them is according to two methods: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for that with fire, make a concave iron cautery similar to a vulture's feather:  which should be made of iron, according to the size which contains the nail on every side: and let it have thin edges.
Then place it, ignited, upon the nail. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the nail, until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and leave it for three days, until it begins to emit pus. Then plaster it with wild mallows, crushed with salt: and leave the plaster on it at night. Then it itself will be eradicated from its roots.
